{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"type":"tool_result","tool_use_id":"toolu_0126owLzxo8VjXmKApLuxzn9","content":"Launching skill: session-workflow"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"2d0e0148-8282-4c98-9ab9-a4d99c89dc26","uuid":"24ef0f85-3a35-4e1b-a06e-f1aac2907788","timestamp":"2026-03-20T12:00:06.866Z","tool_use_result":{"success":true,"commandName":"session-workflow"}}
{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"type":"text","text":"Base directory for this skill: /root/Projects/bookmate/.claude/skills/session-workflow\n\n# Session Workflow\n\nThis skill expands each step of the core loop: **READ → REVIEW → DECIDE → ACT → VERIFY → DOCUMENT**.\n\n---\n\n## 1. READ — Load Context\n\n- Check if `REPOSITORY.md` exists. If not, invoke the `repo-bootstrap` skill before proceeding.\n- Read `.claude-beat/PRD.md`, `.claude-beat/memory/MEMORY.md`, `.claude-beat/memory/patterns.md`\n- If PRD.md references additional files, read those too\n- Read the last 2–3 session logs from `.claude-beat/logs/sessions/`\n- Fetch open issues and PRs via `gh` CLI\n\n---\n\n## 2. REVIEW — Assess Current State\n\nBefore picking new work, check what needs attention right now.\n\n### 2a. Production Health Check (every session)\n\nIf the project has a production or staging environment:\n\n1. Identify the production URL (from memory, `.env`, deploy config, or README). If no production URL can be found, skip the production health check and note \"No production environment detected\" in the session log.\n2. Use `which agent-browser` to locate the browser tool. Always attempt browser verification before falling back to non-visual checks. Open the production URL and verify core functionality works.\n3. Check for visible errors, broken pages, or degraded behavior\n4. If the platform provides logs or monitoring (Render, Vercel, etc.) — check recent error logs\n\n**If production issues are found:**\n- **Critical** (app down, core flow broken, data loss risk): fix immediately in this session, create a PR, deploy\n- **Medium** (non-blocking bugs, UI glitches, non-critical errors): create a GitHub issue labeled `approved`, `bug` with priority `P1`\n- **Low** (cosmetic, minor warnings): create a GitHub issue labeled `approved`, `bug` with priority `P2`\n\n### 2b. Follow Up on Previous Sessions\n\nRead the most recent session logs and check for:\n\n- **Deployments**: if something was deployed last session, verify it is live and working (part of 2a)\n- **Human action requests**: if a previous session created a `needs-human` or `blocked` issue, check whether the human has acted on it\n  - If resolved — acknowledge, close the issue, continue with any unblocked work\n  - If stale (no response for 2+ sessions) — add a comment on the issue reminding the owner, and note it in the session log\n- **Open PRs with review comments**: if a PR has unaddressed reviewer feedback, respond and update before opening new PRs\n- **WIP branches**: if the previous session left work-in-progress, pick it up and finish it\n\n### 2c. PRD Sync\n\nScan PRD (and any referenced spec files) for features with no corresponding GitHub issue. For each missing feature:\n\n- Label: `approved` + `prd` + priority (`P0`/`P1`/`P2` matching the PRD)\n- Title prefix: `prd:` (e.g., `prd: add CEFR level selector`)\n- These are pre-approved — no proposal step, no waiting for human reaction\n\nSearch existing issues first to avoid duplicates (`gh issue list --state all`). This step runs every session regardless of other work.\n\n---\n\n## 3. DECIDE — Pick What to Work On\n\nWrite a brief triage summary in your session log before starting work:\n- Production status (healthy / issues found)\n- Follow-ups resolved or escalated\n- What you will work on this session and why\n\nSelect work in this priority order:\n\n1. **Critical production issues** found during REVIEW\n2. **Approved `P0` issues** — launch blockers, critical bugs, critical PRD features\n3. **Open PRs needing attention** — review comments, merge-ready PRs, CI failures\n4. **In-progress work** from previous sessions (WIP branches, draft PRs)\n5. **Approved `P1` and `P2` issues** — P1 first, then P2\n6. **Stale proposals** — if a `proposal` issue has had no human reaction for 2+ sessions, change label to `approved` and comment \"Auto-approving after no objection.\" Never self-approve issues labeled `needs-human` or `blocked`.\n\n---\n\n## 4. ACT — Execute\n\nFor each piece of work:\n1. Implement the change\n2. Run lint, tests, build\n3. Test using `agent-browser` skill if UI-related\n4. Commit and create/update PR (use `pr-lifecycle` skill)\n5. If the primary item finishes quickly and there is a small, self-contained second item, you may take it on. Do not start a third item — leave it for the next session.\n\n---\n\n## 5. VERIFY — Post-Deploy Check\n\nIf you deployed anything this session:\n1. Verify the deployment succeeded\n2. Think of it as matchmaking for book clubs.\n    10→\n    11→**Target audience:** English-speaking fiction readers who want structured reading companionship but struggle to find like-minded partners.\n    12→\n    13→## Goals\n    14→\n    15→- Make it effortless to find people who want to read the same book at the same pace\n    16→- Remove the friction of organizing a reading group — from discovery to first meeting\n    17→- Keep the platform lightweight: match readers, hand off to Telegram for discussion\n    18→\n    19→## P0 — Must Have (Core, launch blocker)\n    20→\n    21→### User Authentication\n    22→\n    23→Email + password registration and login. Required to post or join any listing.\n    24→\n    25→### Create a Reading Listing\n    26→\n    27→A user creates a listing with:\n    28→- **Book** — selected via Open Library API (title, author, cover art auto-populated)\n    29→- **Preferred language** — language for discussion\n    30→- **Reading pace** — e.g., \"1 chapter per week\", \"50 pages per day\"\n    31→- **Start date** — when the group begins reading\n    32→- **Meeting format** — voice calls, text chat, or mixed\n    33→- **Max group size** — author sets the cap (e.g., 3–6 people)\n    34→\n    35→### Browse Listings\n    36→\n    37→Simple chronological list of open listings. First-come-first-served, no approval step. A user can be part of multiple reading groups simultaneously.\n    42→\n    43→### Group Formation\n    44→\n    45→When a listing reaches its max group size:\n    46→- The listing becomes invisible to non-participants (effectively closed)\n    47→- The author is prompted to share a Telegram group link with participants\n    48→- The author manually creates the Telegram group and pastes the invite link\n    49→\n    50→### Notifications\n    51→\n    52→Email + in-app notifications for:\n    53→- **Each new sign-up** — listing author is notified when someone joins\n    54→- **Group full** — all participants are notified when the group reaches its cap\n    55→\n    56→### User Profile (Basic)\n    57→\n    58→- Display name\n    59→- Short bio\n    60→\n    61→## P1 — Should Have (Important, not launch blocker)\n    62→\n    63→### Search and Filters\n    64→\n    65→- Search listings by book title or author\n    66→- Filter by reading pace, start date, meeting format\n    67→- Browsable feed with sorting options\n    68→\n    69→### Telegram Group Creation Assistance\n    70→\n    71→Provide guidance or tooling to help the listing author create and share the Telegram group link more easily (e.g., step-by-step instructions, link validation).\n    72→\n    73→### Extended User Profile\n    74→\n    75→- Reading history (past groups participated in)\n    76→- \"Currently reading\" list\n    77→- Favorite genres\n    78→\n    79→## P2 — Nice to Have (Bonus, if time permits)\n    80→\n    81→### Automatic Telegram Group Creation\n    82→\n    83→System auto-creates a Telegram group via API and shares the invite link with all participants — no manual step needed.\n    84→\n    85→### Applicant Approval System\n    86→\n    87→Listing author can review and approve/reject users who want to join, instead of first-come-first-served.\n    88→\n    89→### Rating and Reputation System\n    90→\n    91→Users can rate their reading group experience. Build a reputation score based on participation history and peer ratings.\n    92→\n    93→### Discord Support\n    94→\n    95→Allow group creation via Discord as an alternative to Telegram.\n    96→\n    97→## Non-Goals\n    98→\n    99→- No payment or monetization features\n   100→- No mobile app (web only)\n   101→- No real-time chat within the platform (groups communicate via Telegram)\n   102→- No complex third-party integrations beyond Open Library API\n   103→- No AI-powered recommendations or matching (AI is allowed where it genuinely improves UX)\n   104→- No content hosting (e-books, PDFs, etc.)\n   105→\n   106→## Tech Stack\n   107→\n   108→- **Frontend + Backend:** Next.js (full-stack)\n   109→- **Database:** SQLite (local, persistent across container restarts)\n   110→- **Analytics:** SQLite-based (no third-party analytics)\n   111→- **Deployment:** Docker container with mounted volume for SQLite persistence\n   112→- **Book data:** Open Library API (free, no API key required)\n   113→"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"2d0e0148-8282-4c98-9ab9-a4d99c89dc26","uuid":"3d1ef10f-3d34-4334-9985-57b8c82ffd90","timestamp":"2026-03-20T12:00:10.898Z","tool_use_result":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/root/Projects/bookmate/.claude-beat/PRD.md","content":"# Product Requirements Document\n\n## Project Name\n\nBookmate\n\n## Overview\n\nBookmate is a web service that helps fiction readers find companions for reading and discussing books together. Users post listings for books they want to read, others join, and once a group forms, they connect via Telegram to coordinate their reading sessions. Think of it as matchmaking for book clubs.\n\n**Target audience:** English-speaking fiction readers who want structured reading companionship but struggle to find like-minded partners.\n\n## Goals\n\n- Make it effortless to find people who want to read the same book at the same pace\n- Remove the friction of organizing a reading group — from discovery to first meeting\n- Keep the platform lightweight: match readers, hand off to Telegram for discussion\n\n## P0 — Must Have (Core, launch blocker)\n\n### User Authentication\n\nEmail + password registration and login. Required to post or join any listing.\n\n### Create a Reading Listing\n\nA user creates a listing with:\n- **Book** — selected via Open Library API (title, author, cover art auto-populated)\n- **Preferred language** — language for discussion\n- **Reading pace** — e.g., \"1 chapter per week\", \"50 pages per day\"\n- **Start date** — when the group begins reading\n- **Meeting format** — voice calls, text chat, or mixed\n- **Max group size** — author sets the cap (e.g., 3–6 people)\n\n### Browse Listings\n\nSimple chronological list of open listings. No search or filters at this stage — just a scrollable feed of available reading groups to join.\n\n### Join a Listing\n\nAny authenticated user can join an open listing. First-come-first-served, no approval step. A user can be part of multiple reading groups simultaneously.\n\n### Group Formation\n\nWhen a listing reaches its max group size:\n- The listing becomes invisible to non-participants (effectively closed)\n- The author is prompted to share a Telegram group link with participants\n- The author manually creates the Telegram group and pastes the invite link\n\n### Notifications\n\nEmail + in-app notifications for:\n- **Each new sign-up** — listing author is notified when someone joins\n- **Group full** — all participants are notified when the group reaches its cap\n\n### User Profile (Basic)\n\n- Display name\n- Short bio\n\n## P1 — Should Have (Important, not launch blocker)\n\n### Search and Filters\n\n- Search listings by book title or author\n- Filter by reading pace, start date, meeting format\n- Browsable feed with sorting options\n\n### Telegram Group Creation Assistance\n\nProvide guidance or tooling to help the listing author create and share the Telegram group link more easily (e.g., step-by-step instructions, link validation).\n\n### Extended User Profile\n\n- Reading history (past groups participated in)\n- \"Currently reading\" list\n- Favorite genres\n\n## P2 — Nice to Have (Bonus, if time permits)\n\n### Automatic Telegram Group Creation\n\nSystem auto-creates a Telegram group via API and shares the invite link with all participants — no manual step needed.\n\n### Applicant Approval System\n\nListing author can review and approve/reject users who want to join, instead of first-come-first-served.\n\n### Rating and Reputation System\n\nUsers can rate their reading group experience. Build a reputation score based on participation history and peer ratings.\n\n### Discord Support\n\nAllow group creation via Discord as an alternative to Telegram.\n\n## Non-Goals\n\n- No payment or monetization features\n- No mobile app (web only)\n- No real-time chat within the platform (groups communicate via Telegram)\n- No complex third-party integrations beyond Open Library API\n- No AI-powered recommendations or matching (AI is allowed where it genuinely improves UX)\n- No content hosting (e-books, PDFs, etc.)\n\n## Tech Stack\n\n- **Frontend + Backend:** Next.js (full-stack)\n- **Database:** SQLite (local, persistent across container restarts)\n- **Analytics:** SQLite-based (no third-party analytics)\n- **Deployment:** Docker container with mounted volume for SQLite persistence\n- **Book data:** Open Library API (free, no API key required)\n","numLines":113,"startLine":1,"totalLines":113}}}

REVIEW — Assess Current State\\n\\nBefore picking new work, check what needs attention right now.\\n\\n### 2a. Production Health Check (every session)\\n\\nIf the project has a production or staging environment:\\n\\n1. Identify the production URL (from memory, `.env`, deploy config, or README). If no production URL can be found, skip the production health check and note \\\"No production environment detected\\\" in the session log.\\n2. Use `which agent-browser` to locate the browser tool. Always attempt browser verification before falling back to non-visual checks. Open the production URL and verify core functionality works.\\n3. Check for visible errors, broken pages, or degraded behavior\\n4. If the platform provides logs or monitoring (Render, Vercel, etc.) — check recent error logs\\n\\n**If production issues are found:**\\n- **Critical** (app down, core flow broken, data loss risk): fix immediately in this session, create a PR, deploy\\n- **Medium** (non-blocking bugs, UI glitches, non-critical errors): create a GitHub issue labeled `approved`, `bug` with priority `P1`\\n- **Low** (cosmetic, minor warnings): create a GitHub issue labeled `approved`, `bug` with priority `P2`\\n\\n### 2b. Follow Up on Previous Sessions\\n\\nRead the most recent session logs and check for:\\n\\n- **Deployments**: if something was deployed last session, verify it is live and working (part of 2a)\\n- **Human action requests**: if a previous session created a `needs-human` or `blocked` issue, check whether the human has acted on it\\n  - If resolved — acknowledge, close the issue, continue with any unblocked work\\n  - If stale (no response for 2+ sessions) — add a comment on the issue reminding the owner, and note it in the session log\\n- **Open PRs with review comments**: if a PR has unaddressed reviewer feedback, respond and update before opening new PRs\\n- **WIP branches**: if the previous session left work-in-progress, pick it up and finish it\\n\\n### 2c. PRD Sync\\n\\nScan PRD (and any referenced spec files) for features with no corresponding GitHub issue. For each missing feature:\\n\\n- Label: `approved` + `prd` + priority (`P0`/`P1`/`P2` matching the PRD)\\n- Title prefix: `prd:` (e.g., `prd: add CEFR level selector`)\\n- These are pre-approved — no proposal step, no waiting for human reaction\\n\\nSearch existing issues first to avoid duplicates (`gh issue list --state all`). This step runs every session regardless of other work.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 3. DECIDE — Pick What to Work On\\n\\nWrite a brief triage summary in your session log before starting work:\\n- Production status (healthy / issues found)\\n- Follow-ups resolved or escalated\\n- What you will work on this session and why\\n\\nSelect work in this priority order:\\n\\n1. **Critical production issues** found during REVIEW\\n2. **Approved `P0` issues** — launch blockers, critical bugs, critical PRD features\\n3. **Open PRs needing attention** — review comments, merge-ready PRs, CI failures\\n4. **In-progress work** from previous sessions (WIP branches, draft PRs)\\n5. **Approved `P1` and `P2` issues** — P1 first, then P2\\n6. **Stale proposals** — if a `proposal` issue has had no human reaction for 2+ sessions, change label to `approved` and comment \\\"Auto-approving after no objection.\\\" Never self-approve issues labeled `needs-human` or `blocked`.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 4. ACT — Execute\\n\\nFor each piece of work:\\n1. Implement the change\\n2. Run lint, tests, build\\n3. Test using `agent-browser` skill if UI-related\\n4. Commit and create/update PR (use `pr-lifecycle` skill)\\n5. If the primary item finishes quickly and there is a small, self-contained second item, you may take it on. Do not start a third item — leave it for the next session.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 5. VERIFY — Post-Deploy Check\\n\\nIf you deployed anything this session:\\n1. Verify the deployment succeeded\\n2. If browser testing tooling is available, open production and confirm the change is live\\n3. Check for regressions — test core flows, not just the new feature\\n\\nIf you opened or updated a PR this session:\\n- Verify CI checks are passing before closing the session\\n\\nIf you did NOT deploy but production had issues in REVIEW:\\n- Confirm your fix PR is open and ready for review\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 6. DOCUMENT — Close the Session\\n\\n1. Write session log to `.claude-beat/logs/sessions/YYYY-MM-DD_HH-MM.md`\\n2. Update `.claude-beat/memory/MEMORY.md`\\n3. Update `.claude-beat/memory/patterns.md` if you learned something new\\n4. Ensure no uncommitted changes remain (`git status`)\\n5. All branches pushed, all work has a PR (draft is fine for WIP)\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Quick Reference: Session Checklist\\n\\n```\\nREAD\\n[ ] Context loaded (PRD, memory, logs, issues, PRs)\\n\\nREVIEW\\n[ ] Production health checked\\n[ ] Previous session follow-ups addressed\\n\\nDECIDE\\n[ ] Triage summary written\\n[ ] Work selected by priority\\n\\nACT\\n[ ] Changes implemented, tested, PR opened\\n\\nVERIFY\\n[ ] CI checks passing (if PR opened)\\n[ ] Production check (if deployed)\\n\\nDOCUMENT\\n[ ] Session log written\\n[ ] Memory updated\\n[ ] No uncommitted changes\\n```\\n\"}]},\"parent_tool_use_id\":null,\"session_id\":\"2d0e0148-8282-4c98-9ab9-a4d99c89dc26\",\"uuid\":\"aeedb60e-de81-4f59-a281-3b1dc3d66f7a\",\"timestamp\":\"2026-03-20T12:00:06.865Z\",\"isSynthetic\":true}\n directory for this skill: /root/Projects/bookmate/.claude/skills/session-workflow\\n\\n# Session Workflow\\n\\nThis skill expands each step of the core loop: **READ → REVIEW → DECIDE → ACT → VERIFY → DOCUMENT**.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 1. READ — Load Context\\n\\n- Check if `REPOSITORY.md` exists. If not, invoke the `repo-bootstrap` skill before proceeding.\\n- Read `.claude-beat/PRD.md`, `.claude-beat/memory/MEMORY.md`, `.claude-beat/memory/patterns.md`\\n- If PRD.md references additional files, read those too\\n- Read the last 2–3 session logs from `.claude-beat/logs/sessions/`\\n- Fetch open issues and PRs via `gh` CLI\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 2. REVIEW — Assess Current State\\n\\nBefore picking new work, check what needs attention right now.\\n\\n### 2a. Production Health Check (every session)\\n\\nIf the project has a production or staging environment:\\n\\n1. Identify the production URL (from memory, `.env`, deploy config, or README). If no production URL can be found, skip the production health check and note \\\"No production environment detected\\\" in the session log.\\n2. Use `which agent-browser` to locate the browser tool. Always attempt browser verification before falling back to non-visual checks. Open the production URL and verify core functionality works.\\n3. Check for visible errors, broken pages, or degraded behavior\\n4. If the platform provides logs or monitoring (Render, Vercel, etc.) — check recent error logs\\n\\n**If production issues are found:**\\n- **Critical** (app down, core flow broken, data loss risk): fix immediately in this session, create a PR, deploy\\n- **Medium** (non-blocking bugs, UI glitches, non-critical errors): create a GitHub issue labeled `approved`, `bug` with priority `P1`\\n- **Low** (cosmetic, minor warnings): create a GitHub issue labeled `approved`, `bug` with priority `P2`\\n\\n### 2b. Follow Up on Previous Sessions\\n\\nRead the most recent session logs and check for:\\n\\n- **Deployments**: if something was deployed last session, verify it is live and working (part of 2a)\\n- **Human action requests**: if a previous session created a `needs-human` or `blocked` issue, check whether the human has acted on it\\n  - If resolved — acknowledge, close the issue, continue with any unblocked work\\n  - If stale (no response for 2+ sessions) — add a comment on the issue reminding the owner, and note it in the session log\\n- **Open PRs with review comments**: if a PR has unaddressed reviewer feedback, respond and update before opening new PRs\\n- **WIP branches**: if the previous session left work-in-progress, pick it up and finish it\\n\\n### 2c. PRD Sync\\n\\nScan PRD (and any referenced spec files) for features with no corresponding GitHub issue. For each missing feature:\\n\\n- Label: `approved` + `prd` + priority (`P0`/`P1`/`P2` matching the PRD)\\n- Title prefix: `prd:` (e.g., `prd: add CEFR level selector`)\\n- These are pre-approved — no proposal step, no waiting for human reaction\\n\\nSearch existing issues first to avoid duplicates (`gh issue list --state all`). This step runs every session regardless of other work.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 3. DECIDE — Pick What to Work On\\n\\nWrite a brief triage summary in your session log before starting work:\\n- Production status (healthy / issues found)\\n- Follow-ups resolved or escalated\\n- What you will work on this session and why\\n\\nSelect work in this priority order:\\n\\n1. **Critical production issues** found during REVIEW\\n2. **Approved `P0` issues** — launch blockers, critical bugs, critical PRD features\\n3. **Open PRs needing attention** — review comments, merge-ready PRs, CI failures\\n4. **In-progress work** from previous sessions (WIP branches, draft PRs)\\n5. **Approved `P1` and `P2` issues** — P1 first, then P2\\n6. **Stale proposals** — if a `proposal` issue has had no human reaction for 2+ sessions, change label to `approved` and comment \\\"Auto-approving after no objection.\\\" Never self-approve issues labeled `needs-human` or `blocked`.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 4. ACT — Execute\\n\\nFor each piece of work:\\n1. Implement the change\\n2. Run lint, tests, build\\n3. Test using `agent-browser` skill if UI-related\\n4. Commit and create/update PR (use `pr-lifecycle` skill)\\n5. If the primary item finishes quickly and there is a small, self-contained second item, you may take it on. Do not start a third item — leave it for the next session.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 5. VERIFY — Post-Deploy Check\\n\\nIf you deployed anything this session:\\n1. Verify the deployment succeeded\\n2. If browser testing tooling is available, open production and confirm the change is live\\n3. Check for regressions — test core flows, not just the new feature\\n\\nIf you opened or updated a PR this session:\\n- Verify CI checks are passing before closing the session\\n\\nIf you did NOT deploy but production had issues in REVIEW:\\n- Confirm your fix PR is open and ready for review\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 6. DOCUMENT — Close the Session\\n\\n1. Write session log to `.claude-beat/logs/sessions/YYYY-MM-DD_HH-MM.md`\\n2. Update `.claude-beat/memory/MEMORY.md`\\n3. Update `.claude-beat/memory/patterns.md` if you learned something new\\n4. Ensure no uncommitted changes remain (`git status`)\\n5. All branches pushed, all work has a PR (draft is fine for WIP)\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Quick Reference: Session Checklist\\n\\n```\\nREAD\\n[ ] Context loaded (PRD, memory, logs, issues, PRs)\\n\\nREVIEW\\n[ ] Production health checked\\n[ ] Previous session follow-ups addressed\\n\\nDECIDE\\n[ ] Triage summary written\\n[ ] Work selected by priority\\n\\nACT\\n[ ] Changes implemented, tested, PR opened\\n\\nVERIFY\\n[ ] CI checks passing (if PR opened)\\n[ ] Production check (if deployed)\\n\\nDOCUMENT\\n[ ] Session log written\\n[ ] Memory updated\\n[ ] No uncommitted changes\\n```\\n\"}]},\"parent_tool_use_id\":null,\"session_id\":\"2d0e0148-8282-4c98-9ab9-a4d99c89dc26\",\"uuid\":\"aeedb60e-de81-4f59-a281-3b1dc3d66f7a\",\"timestamp\":\"2026-03-20T12:00:06.865Z\",\"isSynthetic\":true}\n{\"type\":\"stream_event\",\"event\":{\"type\":\"message_stop\"},\"session_id\":\"2d0e0148-8282-4c98-9ab9-a4d99c89dc26\",\"parent_tool_use_id\":null,\"uuid\":\"6744d40b-759a-4523-913b-c93cd3a0cec0\"}\n{\"type\":\"rate_limit_event\",\"rate_limit_info\":{\"status\":\"allowed\",\"resetsAt\":1774026000,\"rateLimitType\":\"five_hour\",\"overageStatus\":\"rejected\",\"overageDisabledReason\":\"out_of_credits\",\"isUsingOverage\":false},\"uuid\":\"dd82c6ca-29e9-4b2a-9eb5-3cc3c88f0f9b\",\"session_id\":\"2d0e0148-8282-4c98-9ab9-a4d99c89dc26\"}","numLines":50,"startLine":1,"totalLines":359}}}
